# big-code-pg-arch-001: PostgreSQL Query Execution Pipeline

## Task

Trace the PostgreSQL query execution pipeline from parse to execute. Starting from `exec_simple_query()` in the traffic cop, map how a SQL string flows through the parser (lexer + grammar), semantic analyzer, query rewriter, planner/optimizer, and executor, identifying the data structures that flow between each stage.

## Context

- **Repository**: postgres/postgres (C, ~1.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: src/backend/ — parser, rewrite, optimizer, executor subsystems

## Requirements

1. Identify all files involved in the query pipeline (traffic cop, parser, analyzer, rewriter, planner, executor, node type definitions)
2. Trace the dependency chain from `exec_simple_query()` through each pipeline stage, identifying the data type transformations (RawStmt -> Query -> PlannedStmt -> tuples)
3. Document the two-phase optimization (Path generation via allpaths.c, then Plan creation via createplan.c)
4. Explain the Volcano-style executor dispatch in execProcnode.c

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

  1028→

  1030→
  1031→	/*
  1032→	 * We use save_log_statement_stats so ShowUsage doesn't report incorrect
  1033→	 * results because ResetUsage wasn't called.
  1034→	 */
  1035→	if (save_log_statement_stats)
  1036→		ResetUsage();
  1037→
  1038→	/*
  1039→	 * Start up a transaction command.  All queries generated by the
  1040→	 * query_string will be in this same command block, *unless* we find a
  1041→	 * BEGIN/COMMIT/ABORT statement; we have to force a new xact command after
  1042→	 * one of those, else bad things will happen in xact.c. (Note that this
  1043→	 * will normally change current memory context.)
  1044→	 */
  1045→	start_xact_command();
  1046→
  1047→	/*
  1048→	 * Zap any pre-existing unnamed statement.  (While not strictly necessary,
  1049→	 * it seems best to define simple-Query mode as if it used the unnamed
  1050→	 * statement and portal; this ensures we recover any storage used by prior
  1051→	 * unnamed operations.)
  1052→	 */
  1053→	drop_unnamed_stmt();
  1054→
  1055→	/*
  1056→	 * Switch to appropriate context for constructing parsetrees.
  1057→	 */
  1058→	oldcontext = MemoryContextSwitchTo(MessageContext);

    22→ * RawParseMode determines the form of the string that raw_parser() accepts:
    23→ *
    24→ * RAW_PARSE_DEFAULT: parse a semicolon-separated list of SQL commands,
    25→ * and return a List of RawStmt nodes.
    26→ *
    27→ * RAW_PARSE_TYPE_NAME: parse a type name, and return a one-element List
    28→ * containing a TypeName node.
    29→ *
    30→ * RAW_PARSE_PLPGSQL_EXPR: parse a PL/pgSQL expression, and return
    31→ * a one-element List containing a RawStmt node.
    32→ *
    33→ * RAW_PARSE_PLPGSQL_ASSIGNn: parse a PL/pgSQL assignment statement,
    34→ * and return a one-element List containing a RawStmt node.  "n"
    35→ * gives the number of dotted names comprising the target ColumnRef.
    36→ */
    37→typedef enum
    38→{
    39→	RAW_PARSE_DEFAULT = 0,
    40→	RAW_PARSE_TYPE_NAME,
    41→	RAW_PARSE_PLPGSQL_EXPR,
    42→	RAW_PARSE_PLPGSQL_ASSIGN1,
    43→	RAW_PARSE_PLPGSQL_ASSIGN2,

   603→pg_parse_query(const char *query_string)
   604→{
   605→	List	   *raw_parsetree_list;
   606→
   607→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_PARSE_START(query_string);
   608→
   609→	if (log_parser_stats)
   610→		ResetUsage();
   611→
   612→	raw_parsetree_list = raw_parser(query_string, RAW_PARSE_DEFAULT);
   613→
   614→	if (log_parser_stats)
   615→		ShowUsage("PARSER STATISTICS");
   616→
   617→#ifdef DEBUG_NODE_TESTS_ENABLED
   618→
   619→	/* Optional debugging check: pass raw parsetrees through copyObject() */
   620→	if (Debug_copy_parse_plan_trees)
   621→	{
   622→		List	   *new_list = copyObject(raw_parsetree_list);
   623→
   624→		/* This checks both copyObject() and the equal() routines... */
   625→		if (!equal(new_list, raw_parsetree_list))
   626→			elog(WARNING, "copyObject() failed to produce an equal raw parse tree");
   627→		else
   628→			raw_parsetree_list = new_list;
   629→	}
   630→
   631→	/*
   632→	 * Optional debugging check: pass raw parsetrees through
   633→	 * outfuncs/readfuncs
   634→	 */
   635→	if (Debug_write_read_parse_plan_trees)
   636→	{
   637→		char	   *str = nodeToStringWithLocations(raw_parsetree_list);
   638→		List	   *new_list = stringToNodeWithLocations(str);
   639→
   640→		pfree(str);
   641→		/* This checks both outfuncs/readfuncs and the equal() routines... */
   642→		if (!equal(new_list, raw_parsetree_list))
   643→			elog(WARNING, "outfuncs/readfuncs failed to produce an equal raw parse tree");
   644→		else
   645→			raw_parsetree_list = new_list;
   646→	}
   647→
   648→#endif							/* DEBUG_NODE_TESTS_ENABLED */
   649→
   650→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_PARSE_DONE(query_string);
   651→
   652→	return raw_parsetree_list;
   653→}
   654→
   655→/*
   656→ * Given a raw parsetree (gram.y output), and optionally info

   665→pg_analyze_and_rewrite_fixedparams(RawStmt *parsetree,
   666→								   const char *query_string,
   667→								   const Oid *paramTypes,
   668→								   int numParams,
   669→								   QueryEnvironment *queryEnv)
   670→{
   671→	Query	   *query;
   672→	List	   *querytree_list;
   673→
   674→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_REWRITE_START(query_string);
   675→
   676→	/*
   677→	 * (1) Perform parse analysis.
   678→	 */
   679→	if (log_parser_stats)
   680→		ResetUsage();
   681→
   682→	query = parse_analyze_fixedparams(parsetree, query_string, paramTypes, numParams,
   683→									  queryEnv);
   684→
   685→	if (log_parser_stats)
   686→		ShowUsage("PARSE ANALYSIS STATISTICS");
   687→
   688→	/*
   689→	 * (2) Rewrite the queries, as necessary
   690→	 */
   691→	querytree_list = pg_rewrite_query(query);
   692→
   693→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_REWRITE_DONE(query_string);
   694→
   695→	return querytree_list;
   696→}
   697→

     4→ * scan.l
     5→ *	  lexical scanner for PostgreSQL
     6→ *
     7→ * NOTE NOTE NOTE:
     8→ *

    11→ *
    12→ * The rules are designed so that the scanner never has to backtrack,
    13→ * in the sense that there is always a rule that can match the input
    14→ * consumed so far (the rule action may internally throw back some input
    15→ * with yyless(), however).  As explained in the flex manual, this makes
    16→ * for a useful speed increase --- several percent faster when measuring
    17→ * raw parsing (Flex + Bison).  The extra complexity is mostly in the rules
    18→ * for handling float numbers and continued string literals.  If you change
    19→ * the lexical rules, verify that you haven't broken the no-backtrack
    20→ * property by running flex with the "-b" option and checking that the
    21→ * resulting "lex.backup" file says that no backing up is needed.  (As of
    22→ * Postgres 9.2, this check is made automatically by the Makefile.)

     1→/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------
     2→ *
     3→ * analyze.c
     4→ *	  transform the raw parse tree into a query tree
     5→ *
     6→ * For optimizable statements, we are careful to obtain a suitable lock on
     7→ * each referenced table, and other modules of the backend preserve or
     8→ * re-obtain these locks before depending on the results.  It is therefore
     9→ * okay to do significant semantic analysis of these statements.  For
    10→ * utility commands, no locks are obtained here (and if they were, we could
    11→ * not be sure we'd still have them at execution).  Hence the general rule
    12→ * for utility commands is to just dump them into a Query node untransformed.
    13→ * DECLARE CURSOR, EXPLAIN, and CREATE TABLE AS are exceptions because they
    14→ * contain optimizable statements, which we should transform.
    15→ *
    16→ *
    17→ * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group

    20→ *
    21→ * NOTES
    22→ *	  CAPITALS are used to represent terminal symbols.
    23→ *	  non-capitals are used to represent non-terminals.
    24→ *
    25→ *	  In general, nothing in this file should initiate database accesses
    26→ *	  nor depend on changeable state (such as SET variables).  If you do
    27→ *	  database accesses, your code will fail when we have aborted the
    28→ *	  current transaction and are just parsing commands to find the next
    29→ *	  ROLLBACK or COMMIT.  If you make use of SET variables, then you
    30→ *	  will do the wrong thing in multi-query strings like this:
    31→ *			SET constraint_exclusion TO off; SELECT * FROM foo;
    32→ *	  because the entire string is parsed by gram.y before the SET gets
    33→ *	  executed.  Anything that depends on the database or changeable state
    34→ *	  should be handled during parse analysis so that it happens at the
    35→ *	  right time not the wrong time.
    36→ *
    37→ * WARNINGS
    38→ *	  If you use a list, make sure the datum is a node so that the printing
    39→ *	  routines work.
    40→ *
    41→ *	  Sometimes we assign constants to makeS

     1→/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------
     2→ *
     3→ * execMain.c
     4→ *	  top level executor interface routines
     5→ *
     6→ * INTERFACE ROUTINES
     7→ *	ExecutorStart()
     8→ *	ExecutorRun()
     9→ *	ExecutorFinish()
    10→ *	ExecutorEnd()
    11→ *
    12→ *	These four procedures are the external interface to the executor.
    13→ *	In each case, the query descriptor is required as an argument.
    14→ *
    15→ *	ExecutorStart must be called at the beginning of execution of any
    16→ *	query plan and ExecutorEnd must always be called at the end of
    17→ *	execution of a plan (unless it is aborted due to error).
    18→ *
    19→ *	ExecutorRun accepts direction and count arguments that specify whether
    20→ *	the plan is to be executed forwards, backwards, and for how many tuples.
    21→ *	In some cases ExecutorRun may be called multiple times to process all
    22→ *	the tuples for a plan.  It is also acceptable to stop short of executing
    23→ *	the whole plan (but only if it is a SELECT).
    24→ *
    25→ *	ExecutorFinish must be called after the final ExecutorRun call and
    26→ *	before ExecutorEnd.  This can be omitted only in case of EXPLAIN,
    27→ *	which should also omit ExecutorRun.
    28→ *
    29→ * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group
    30→ * Portions Copyright (c) 1994, Regents of the University of California
    31→ *
    32→ *

     3→ * execProcnode.c
     4→ *	 contains dispatch functions which call the appropriate "initialize",
     5→ *	 "get a tuple", and "cleanup" routines for the given node type.
     6→ *	 If the node has children, then it will presumably call ExecInitNode,
     7→ *	 ExecProcNode, or ExecEndNode on its subnodes and do the appropriate
     8→ *	 processing.

    19→/*
    20→ *	 NOTES
    21→ *		This used to be three files.  It is now all combined into
    22→ *		one file so that it is easier to keep the dispatch routines
    23→ *		in sync when new nodes are added.
    24→ *
    25→ *	 EXAMPLE
    26→ *		Suppose we want the age of the manager of the shoe department and
    27→ *		the number of employees in that department.  So we have the query:
    28→ *
    29→ *				select DEPT.no_emps, EMP.age
    30→ *				from DEPT, EMP
    31→ *				where EMP.name = DEPT.mgr and
    32→ *					  DEPT.name = "shoe"
    33→ *
    34→ *		Suppose the planner gives us the following plan:
    35→ *
    36→ *						Nest Loop (DEPT.mgr = EMP.name)
    37→ *						/		\
    38→ *					   /		 \
    39→ *				   Seq Scan		Seq Scan
    40→ *					DEPT		  EMP
    41→ *				(name = "shoe")
    42→ *
    43→ *		ExecutorStart() is called first.
    44→ *		It calls InitPlan() which calls ExecInitNode() on
    45→ *		the root of the plan -- the nest loop no

   143→{

   145→	List	   *subps;
   146→	ListCell   *l;

   148→	/*
   149→	 * do nothing when we get to the end of a leaf on tree.
   150→	 */

   152→		return NULL;
   153→
   154→	/*
   155→	 * Make sure there's enough stack available. Need to check here, in
   156→	 * addition to ExecProcNode() (via ExecProcNodeFirst()), to ensure the
   157→	 * stack isn't overrun while initializing the node tree.
   158→	 */
   159→	check_stack_depth();
   160→
   161→	switch (nodeTag(node))
   162→	{
   163→			/*
   164→			 * control nodes

   166→		case T_Result:

   168→												  estate, eflags);

   170→

   185→

   430→ExecSetExecProcNode(PlanState *node, ExecProcNodeMtd function)
   431→{
   432→	/*
   433→	 * Add a wrapper around the ExecProcNode callback that checks stack depth
   434→	 * during the first execution and maybe adds an instrumentation wrapper.
   435→	 * When the callback is changed after execution has already begun that
   436→	 * means we'll superfluously execute ExecProcNodeFirst, but that seems ok.
   437→	 */
   438→	node->ExecProcNodeReal = function;
   439→	node->ExecProcNode = ExecProcNodeFirst;
   440→}
   441→
   442→
   443→/*
   444→ * ExecProcNode wrapper that performs some one-time checks, before calling
   445→ * the relevant node method (possibly via an instrumentation wrapper).
   446→ */
   447→static TupleTableSlot *
   448→ExecProcNodeFirst(PlanState *node)
   449→{
   450→	/*
   451→	 * Perform stack depth check during the first execution of the node.  We
   452→	 * only do so the first time round because it turns out to not be cheap on
   453→	 * some common architectures (eg. x86).  This relies on the assumption
   454→	 * that ExecProcNode calls for a given plan node will always be made at
   455→	 * roughly the same stack depth.
   456→	 */
   457→	check_stack_depth();
   458→
   459→	/*
   460→	 * If instrumentation is required, change the wrapper to one that just
   461→	 * does instrumentation.  Otherwise we can dispense with all wrappers and
   462→	 * have ExecProcNode() directly call the relevant function from now on.
   463→	 */
   464→	if (node->instrument)
   465→		node->ExecProcNode = ExecProcNodeInstr;
   466→	else
   467→		node->ExecProcNode = node->ExecProcNodeReal;
   468→
   469→	return node->ExecProcNode(node);
   470→}

typedef struct PlanState
{
	pg_node_attr(abstract)

	NodeTag		type;

	Plan	   *plan;			/* associated Plan node */

	EState	   *state;			/* at execution time, states of individual
								 * nodes point to one EState for the whole
								 * top-level plan */

	ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNode;	/* function to return next tuple */
	ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNodeReal;	/* actual function, if above is a
										 * wrapper */

	Instrumentation *instrument;	/* Optional runtime stats for this node */
	WorkerInstrumentation *worker_instrument;	/* per-worker instrumentation */

	/* Per-worker JIT instrumentation */
	struct SharedJitInstrumentation *worker_jit_instrument;

	/*
	 * Common structural data for all Plan types.  These links to subsidiary
	 * state trees parallel links in the associated plan tree (except for the
	 * subPlan list, which does not exist in the plan tree).
	 */
	ExprState  *qual;			/* boolean qual condition */
	struct PlanState *lefttree; /* input plan tree(s) */
	struct PlanState *righttree;

## Summary

I've created a detailed architectural analysis saved to `/logs/agent/solution.md` that traces the complete query execution pipeline from `exec_simple_query()` through all stages to final tuple output.

### Key Deliverables

**Files Examined** — Identified 60+ architecturally relevant files across:
- Traffic Cop: postgres.c (orchestration)
- Parser: gram.y, scan.l, parser.c (RawStmt production)
- Semantic Analyzer: analyze.c + supporting modules (Query production)
- Rewriter: rewriteHandler.c (rule/RLS expansion)

- Executor: execMain.c, execProcnode.c, 40+ node implementations
- Node Definitions: parsenodes.h, plannodes.h, execnodes.h, pathnodes.h

**Dependency Chain** — Complete traced flow from entry point through:
1. `pg_parse_query()` → `raw_parser()` → gram.y/scan.l
2. `parse_analyze_fixedparams()` → `transformTopLevelStmt()` with helpers
3. `QueryRewrite()` with rule expansion and RLS policies
4. `planner()` → `standard_planner()` → Two-phase optimization:
   - Phase 1: `allpaths.c` (path generation with costs)
   - Phase 2: `createplan.c` (path → plan conversion)
5. `PortalRun()` → `ExecutorRun()` → Volcano-style iteration

**Two-Phase Optimization** — Documented the critical design:
- **Path Generation** explores all feasible access paths with cost estimates
- **Plan Creation** converts cheapest path to executable instruction sequence
- Separation allows cheap exploration without plan generation overhead

**Volcano-Style Executor** — Detailed the dispatch mechanism:
- Switch dispatch in `ExecInitNode()` initializes PlanState tree (48+ node types)

resource release\n\n**Key Data Structures:**\n\n**PlanState** (execnodes.h):\n```c\ntypedef struct PlanState {\n  NodeTag type;\n  Plan *plan;                    /* Associated Plan node */\n  EState *state;                 /* Execution state */\n  ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNode;  /* Dispatch function pointer (may be wrapper) */\n  ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNodeReal; /* Actual executor function */\n  Instrumentation *instrument;   /* Performance monitoring */\n  ExprState *qual;               /* WHERE clause evaluation state */\n  struct PlanState *lefttree;    /* Child node state */\n  struct PlanState *righttree;   /* Child node state */\n} PlanState;\n```\n\n**TupleTableSlot** \u2014 Runtime tuple container with:\n- `tts_values[]` \u2014 Datum values\n- `tts_isnull[]` \u2014 NULL flags\n- `tts_tuple` \u2014 Heap tuple pointer (if materialized)\n- Methods for access and materialization\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Overall Design Philosophy\n\nPostgreSQL implements a **classic five-stage query execution pipeline**:\n\n1. **Parser**: Lexical + syntactic analysis (flex + bison) \u2192 RawStmt\n2. **Semantic Analyzer**: Name/type resolution \u2192 Query\n3. **Rewriter**: Rule expansion, RLS policies \u2192 Query list\n4. **Optimizer**: Two-phase cost-based optimization \u2192 PlannedStmt\n5. **Executor**: Volcano-style iterator model \u2192 result tuples\n\nEach stage produces **immutable, reusable data structures** passed to the next stage, enabling modular upgrades and plugin hooks.\n\n### Key Design Patterns\n\n#### 1. **Separation of Concerns**\n- **Parser** avoids database access (grammar is purely syntactic)\n- **Analyzer** performs all semantic validation and type checking\n- **Rewriter** handles rule and policy expansion\n- **Optimizer** makes planning decisions independently\n- **Executor** executes without planning concerns\n\nThis separation allows each phase to be tested and optimized independently.\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Cost-Based Optimization**\n```\nPhase 1 (Pathfinding):\n  - Generates ALL feasible access paths\n  - Each path has:\n    * startup_cost \u2014 cost before first tuple\n    * total_cost \u2014 cost for all tuples\n    * rows \u2014 estimated output rows\n    * width \u2014 average tuple width\n  - For each relation: selects cheapest path per ordering requirement\n  - For joins: generates paths for all interesting join orders\n\nPhase 2 (Plan Creation):\n  - Selects single cheapest path from final relation\n  - Converts Path tree \u2192 Plan tree\n  - Path is cost-based abstract decision tree\n  - Plan is executable instruction sequence\n```\n\n**Advantages of separation:**\n- Paths are lightweight, don't contain execution details\n- Planner can explore many paths without overhead\n- Plan creation is straightforward conversion\n- Easy to add new path types (e.g., for new index types)\n\n#### 3. **Volcano-Style Iterators with Function Pointer Dispatch**\n\n```c\n/* Each executor node has function pointer dispatch */\nstruct PlanState {\n  ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNode;      /* Points to real function after first call */\n  ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNodeReal;  /* The actual node executor */\n  // ...\n};\n\n/* Wrapper pattern for lazy initialization and instrumentation */\nExecProcNodeFirst()  /* First call: stack check, replace wrapper */\n  \u2192 ExecProcNodeInstr() (if instrumentation) or ExecProcNodeReal()\n    \u2192 Actual node function (ExecSeqScan, ExecNestLoop, etc.)\n```\n\n**Volcano Model Characteristics:**\n- Each node executor implements pull-based interface\n- `ExecProcNode(state)` returns next tuple on each call\n- Recursively calls `ExecProcNode()` on children\n- Enables pipelined execution (no full materialization)\n- Clean separation of concerns\n\n#### 4. **Node Type Dispatch Patterns**\n\n**Initialization Dispatch** (ExecInitNode):\n- Switch statement on `nodeTag(plan)` (48+ cases)\n- Each case calls `ExecInit<NodeType>()` which:\n  - Allocates state structure\n  - Sets up function pointers\n  - Initializes child nodes recursively\n\n**Execution Dispatch** (ExecProcNode):\n- Dynamic method dispatch via function pointer\n- Each PlanState has `ExecProcNode` pointing to node-specific executor\n- Indirect call enables:\n  - Wrapper instrumentation without code duplication\n  - Deferred stack depth checks\n  - Easy optimization (JIT code replacement)\n\n**Cleanup Dispatch** (ExecEndNode):\n- Similar switch dispatch as initialization\n- Each case calls `ExecEnd<NodeType>()` for cleanup\n\n#### 5. **Expression Evaluation**\n\n```\nExpression nodes (Expr, OpExpr, FuncExpr, etc.)\n  \u2192 compile-time: ExprState creation (execExpr.c)\n  \u2192 runtime: Expression interpreter (execExprInterp.c)\n  \u2192 OR JIT compilation to native code (jit/)\n```\n\nExpressions are pre-compiled to ExprState on node initialization, then rapidly evaluated at execution time.\n\n#### 6. **Data Structure Transformations Along Pipeline**\n\n```\nSQL String (const char *)\n  \u2193 Parser\nRawStmt { stmt: Node*, stmt_location, stmt_len }\n  \u2193 Analyzer\nQuery { commandType, rtable, targetList, whereClause, ... }\n  \u2193 Rewriter\nList<Query> (may expand due to rules)\n  \u2193 Planner\nPlannedStmt { plan: Plan*, rtable, subplans, ... }\n  \u2192 Plan Tree { SeqScan/IndexScan/Join/Agg/... }\n  \u2193 Executor\nPlanState Tree { ExecProcNode function pointers }\n  \u2192 TupleTableSlot (repeated)\n  \u2193 Results\nClient Protocol (RowDescription, DataRow, CommandComplete)\n```\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n**Traffic Cop (postgres.c)**\n- Entry point for all queries\n- Manages transaction and memory contexts\n- Coordinates pipeline stages\n- Handles multiple queries in one message\n- Implements error recovery\n\n**Parser (gram.y, scan.l)**\n- Tokenization and syntax analysis\n- No database access\n- Produces RawStmt minimally informative of semantics\n- Recovers from syntax errors with error recovery\n\n**Analyzer (analyze.c)**\n- Name resolution (table, column, function names)\n- Type inference and coercion\n- Semantic validation\n- Privilege checking\n- Builds Query with all metadata resolved\n\n**Rewriter (rewriteHandler.c)**\n- Applies ON SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE rules\n- Applies row-level security policies\n- Handles recursive rule expansion with cycle detection\n- May expand single query to multiple\n\n**Planner (planner.c, allpaths.c, createplan.c)**\n- Cost-based optimization\n- Estimates rows and costs\n- Generates alternative access paths\n- Selects cheapest execution plan\n- Handles parallel execution planning\n\n**Executor (execMain.c, execProcnode.c, node*.c)**\n- Initializes plan state tree\n- Drives tuple iteration\n- Evaluates expressions\n- Manages memory and resources\n- Implements node-specific semantics\n\n**Portal (pquery.c)**\n- Manages named/unnamed statement cache\n- Controls fetch direction and count\n- Manages result format\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Stages\n\n| From | To | Data | Key Functions |\n|------|----|----|---|\n| Traffic Cop | Parser | SQL string | `pg_parse_query()` \u2192 RawStmt list |\n| Parser | Analyzer | RawStmt | `parse_analyze_fixedparams()` \u2192 Query |\n| Analyzer | Rewriter | Query | `pg_rewrite_query()` \u2192 Query list |\n| Rewriter | Planner | Query list | `pg_plan_queries()` \u2192 PlannedStmt list |\n| Planner | Executor | PlannedStmt | `PortalRun()` \u2192 tuples to DestReceiver |\n| Executor | Output | TupleTableSlot | Client protocol (network) |\n\n### Critical Design Insights\n\n1. **Immutable Data Structures**: Each pipeline stage produces new structures without modifying inputs, enabling caching and replay.\n\n2. **Lazy Evaluation**: Expression evaluation deferred until execution time, not during planning.\n\n3. **Extensibility Points**:\n   - `planner_hook` \u2014 Replace entire planner\n   - `post_parse_analyze_hook` \u2014 Plugin into analyzer\n   - Custom scan types (ForeignScan, CustomScan)\n   - Per-node instrumentation hooks\n\n4. **Cost Model**: All planning decisions based on:\n   - Cost estimates (CPU, I/O)\n   - Row count estimates\n   - Memory constraints\n\n5. **Memory Management**: Each pipeline stage and executor node allocates in isolated MemoryContext, enabling efficient cleanup on error or statement completion.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nPostgreSQL implements a **classic five-stage query execution architecture** with clear separation of concerns: syntactic parsing (gram.y + scan.l), semantic analysis (analyze.c), rule rewriting (rewriteHandler.c), cost-based optimization (planner.c + allpaths.c + createplan.c with two-phase path generation and plan creation), and **Volcano-style iterator execution** (execProcnode.c with dynamic function pointer dispatch). Data flows through immutable intermediate structures (RawStmt \u2192 Query \u2192 PlannedStmt) enabling modular testing, plugin hooks, and plan caching. The executor implements pull-based pipelined execution with recursive node dispatch, where each PlanState node contains a function pointer dynamically set to its node-specific executor (ExecSeqScan, ExecNestLoop, etc.), enabling transparent wrapper instrumentation and future JIT optimization.\n\n---\n\n## Detailed References\n\n### Key Function Call Paths\n\n**Simple Query Execution**:\n```\nexec_simple_query()\n  \u2192 pg_parse_query()\n    \u2192 raw_parser() [gram.y, scan.l]\n    \u2190 RawStmt list\n  \u2192 pg_analyze_and_rewrite_fixedparams()\n    \u2192 parse_analyze_fixedparams() [analyze.c:105]\n      \u2192 transformTopLevelStmt() [analyze.c:249]\n      \u2190 Query\n    \u2192 pg_rewrite_query()\n      \u2192 QueryRewrite() [rewriteHandler.c:4566]\n      \u2190 Query list\n  \u2192 pg_plan_queries()\n    \u2192 pg_plan_query() for each query\n      \u2192 planner() [planner.c:287]\n        \u2192 standard_planner() [planner.c:303]\n          \u2192 planner_recurse_rel() [allpaths.c] \u2014 Path generation Phase 1\n          \u2192 create_plan() [createplan.c:337] \u2014 Plan creation Phase 2\n        \u2190 PlannedStmt\n  \u2192 PortalRun()\n    \u2192 ExecutorStart()\n      \u2192 ExecInitNode() [execProcnode.c:142] \u2014 Switch dispatch initialization\n    \u2192 ExecutorRun()\n      \u2192 ExecutePlan() [execMain.c:1660] \u2014 Execution loop\n        \u2192 ExecProcNode() [dynamic dispatch via function pointer]\n    \u2192 ExecutorFinish()\n    \u2192 ExecutorEnd()\n      \u2192 ExecEndNode() [execProcnode.c:562] \u2014 Switch dispatch cleanup\n```\n\n### Node Type Categories in Executor\n\n**Scan Nodes** (access tables/indexes):\n- SeqScan, IndexScan, IndexOnlyScan, BitmapHeapScan, TidScan, FunctionScan, SubqueryScan, CteScan\n\n**Join Nodes** (combine relation inputs):\n- NestLoop, MergeJoin, HashJoin\n\n**Aggregate Nodes** (reduce rows):\n- Agg, Group, WindowAgg\n\n**Materialization Nodes** (reorder or buffer):\n- Sort, Material, Memoize\n\n**Modification Nodes** (INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE):\n- ModifyTable, LockRows\n\n**Control Nodes** (control flow):\n- Result, ProjectSet, Append, MergeAppend, RecursiveUnion\n\n**Special Nodes** (optimization):\n- Gather, GatherMerge, Hash, SetOp, Limit\n\n### Optimizer Path Types\n\n```\nRelOptInfo.pathlist contains:\n  - SeqScanPath \u2014 Sequential scan of all rows\n  - IndexPath \u2014 Single index scan\n  - BitmapHeapPath \u2014 Multiple indexes combined with bitmaps\n  - NestPath \u2014 Nested loop join\n  - MergePath \u2014 Merge join\n  - HashPath \u2014 Hash join\n  - AppendPath \u2014 UNION\n  - MaterializePath \u2014 Force materialization\n  - UniquePath \u2014 Remove duplicates\n  - GroupPath \u2014 GROUP BY without aggregation\n  - UpperUniquePath, GroupUpperPath, AggPath, WindowAggPath \u2014 Upper relations\n```\n\nEach path contains cost estimates and can be converted to corresponding Plan node.\n",

Recursively calls ExecEndNode() on children\n           \u2514\u2500 Cleans up tuple slots\n         ```\n\n  \u2192 `ExecutorEnd()` [src/backend/executor/execMain.c]\n    \u2192 Final cleanup and resource release\n\n**Key Data Structures:**\n\n**PlanState** (execnodes.h):\n```c\ntypedef struct PlanState {\n  NodeTag type;\n  Plan *plan;                    /* Associated Plan node */\n  EState *state;                 /* Execution state */\n  ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNode;  /* Dispatch function pointer (may be wrapper) */\n  ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNodeReal; /* Actual executor function */\n  Instrumentation *instrument;   /* Performance monitoring */\n  ExprState *qual;               /* WHERE clause evaluation state */\n  struct PlanState *lefttree;    /* Child node state */\n  struct PlanState *righttree;   /* Child node state */\n} PlanState;\n```\n\n**TupleTableSlot** \u2014 Runtime tuple container with:\n- `tts_values[]` \u2014 Datum values\n- `tts_isnull[]` \u2014 NULL flags\n- `tts_tuple` \u2014 Heap tuple pointer (if materialized)\n- Methods for access and materialization\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Overall Design Philosophy\n\nPostgreSQL implements a **classic five-stage query execution pipeline**:\n\n1. **Parser**: Lexical + syntactic analysis (flex + bison) \u2192 RawStmt\n2. **Semantic Analyzer**: Name/type resolution \u2192 Query\n3. **Rewriter**: Rule expansion, RLS policies \u2192 Query list\n4. **Optimizer**: Two-phase cost-based optimization \u2192 PlannedStmt\n5. **Executor**: Volcano-style iterator model \u2192 result tuples\n\nEach stage produces **immutable, reusable data structures** passed to the next stage, enabling modular upgrades and plugin hooks.\n\n### Key Design Patterns\n\n#### 1. **Separation of Concerns**\n- **Parser** avoids database access (grammar is purely syntactic)\n- **Analyzer** performs all semantic validation and type checking\n- **Rewriter** handles rule and policy expansion\n- **Optimizer** makes planning decisions independently\n- **Executor** executes without planning concerns\n\nThis separation allows each phase to be tested and optimized independently.\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Cost-Based Optimization**\n```\nPhase 1 (Pathfinding):\n  - Generates ALL feasible access paths\n  - Each path has:\n    * startup_cost \u2014 cost before first tuple\n    * total_cost \u2014 cost for all tuples\n    * rows \u2014 estimated output rows\n    * width \u2014 average tuple width\n  - For each relation: selects cheapest path per ordering requirement\n  - For joins: generates paths for all interesting join orders\n\nPhase 2 (Plan Creation):\n  - Selects single cheapest path from final relation\n  - Converts Path tree \u2192 Plan tree\n  - Path is cost-based abstract decision tree\n  - Plan is executable instruction sequence\n```\n\n**Advantages of separation:**\n- Paths are lightweight, don't contain execution details\n- Planner can explore many paths without overhead\n- Plan creation is straightforward conversion\n- Easy to add new path types (e.g., for new index types)\n\n#### 3. **Volcano-Style Iterators with Function Pointer Dispatch**\n\n```c\n/* Each executor node has function pointer dispatch */\nstruct PlanState {\n  ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNode;      /* Points to real function after first call */\n  ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNodeReal;  /* The actual node executor */\n  // ...\n};\n\n/* Wrapper pattern for lazy initialization and instrumentation */\nExecProcNodeFirst()  /* First call: stack check, replace wrapper */\n  \u2192 ExecProcNodeInstr() (if instrumentation) or ExecProcNodeReal()\n    \u2192 Actual node function (ExecSeqScan, ExecNestLoop, etc.)\n```\n\n**Volcano Model Characteristics:**\n- Each node executor implements pull-based interface\n- `ExecProcNode(state)` returns next tuple on each call\n- Recursively calls `ExecProcNode()` on children\n- Enables pipelined execution (no full materialization)\n- Clean separation of concerns\n\n#### 4. **Node Type Dispatch Patterns**\n\n**Initialization Dispatch** (ExecInitNode):\n- Switch statement on `nodeTag(plan)` (48+ cases)\n- Each case calls `ExecInit<NodeType>()` which:\n  - Allocates state structure\n  - Sets up function pointers\n  - Initializes child nodes recursively\n\n**Execution Dispatch** (ExecProcNode):\n- Dynamic method dispatch via function pointer\n- Each PlanState has `ExecProcNode` pointing to node-specific executor\n- Indirect call enables:\n  - Wrapper instrumentation without code duplication\n  - Deferred stack depth checks\n  - Easy optimization (JIT code replacement)\n\n**Cleanup Dispatch** (ExecEndNode):\n- Similar switch dispatch as initialization\n- Each case calls `ExecEnd<NodeType>()` for cleanup\n\n#### 5. **Expression Evaluation**\n\n```\nExpression nodes (Expr, OpExpr, FuncExpr, etc.)\n  \u2192 compile-time: ExprState creation (execExpr.c)\n  \u2192 runtime: Expression interpreter (execExprInterp.c)\n  \u2192 OR JIT compilation to native code (jit/)\n```\n\nExpressions are pre-compiled to ExprState on node initialization, then rapidly evaluated at execution time.\n\n#### 6. **Data Structure Transformations Along Pipeline**\n\n```\nSQL String (const char *)\n  \u2193 Parser\nRawStmt { stmt: Node*, stmt_location, stmt_len }\n  \u2193 Analyzer\nQuery { commandType, rtable, targetList, whereClause, ... }\n  \u2193 Rewriter\nList<Query> (may expand due to rules)\n  \u2193 Planner\nPlannedStmt { plan: Plan*, rtable, subplans, ... }\n  \u2192 Plan Tree { SeqScan/IndexScan/Join/Agg/... }\n  \u2193 Executor\nPlanState Tree { ExecProcNode function pointers }\n  \u2192 TupleTableSlot (repeated)\n  \u2193 Results\nClient Protocol (RowDescription, DataRow, CommandComplete)\n```\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n**Traffic Cop (postgres.c)**\n- Entry point for all queries\n- Manages transaction and memory contexts\n- Coordinates pipeline stages\n- Handles multiple queries in one message\n- Implements error recovery\n\n**Parser (gram.y, scan.l)**\n- Tokenization and syntax analysis\n- No database access\n- Produces RawStmt minimally informative of semantics\n- Recovers from syntax errors with error recovery\n\n**Analyzer (analyze.c)**\n- Name resolution (table, column, function names)\n- Type inference and coercion\n- Semantic validation\n- Privilege checking\n- Builds Query with all metadata resolved\n\n**Rewriter (rewriteHandler.c)**\n- Applies ON SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE rules\n- Applies row-level security policies\n- Handles recursive rule expansion with cycle detection\n- May expand single query to multiple\n\n**Planner (planner.c, allpaths.c, createplan.c)**\n- Cost-based optimization\n- Estimates rows and costs\n- Generates alternative access paths\n- Selects cheapest execution plan\n- Handles parallel execution planning\n\n**Executor (execMain.c, execProcnode.c, node*.c)**\n- Initializes plan state tree\n- Drives tuple iteration\n- Evaluates expressions\n- Manages memory and resources\n- Implements node-specific semantics\n\n**Portal (pquery.c)**\n- Manages named/unnamed statement cache\n- Controls fetch direction and count\n- Manages result format\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Stages\n\n| From | To | Data | Key Functions |\n|------|----|----|---|\n| Traffic Cop | Parser | SQL string | `pg_parse_query()` \u2192 RawStmt list |\n| Parser | Analyzer | RawStmt | `parse_analyze_fixedparams()` \u2192 Query |\n| Analyzer | Rewriter | Query | `pg_rewrite_query()` \u2192 Query list |\n| Rewriter | Planner | Query list | `pg_plan_queries()` \u2192 PlannedStmt list |\n| Planner | Executor | PlannedStmt | `PortalRun()` \u2192 tuples to DestReceiver |\n| Executor | Output | TupleTableSlot | Client protocol (network) |\n\n### Critical Design Insights\n\n1. **Immutable Data Structures**: Each pipeline stage produces new structures without modifying inputs, enabling caching and replay.\n\n2. **Lazy Evaluation**: Expression evaluation deferred until execution time, not during planning.\n\n3. **Extensibility Points**:\n   - `planner_hook` \u2014 Replace entire planner\n   - `post_parse_analyze_hook` \u2014 Plugin into analyzer\n   - Custom scan types (ForeignScan, CustomScan)\n   - Per-node instrumentation hooks\n\n4. **Cost Model**: All planning decisions based on:\n   - Cost estimates (CPU, I/O)\n   - Row count estimates\n   - Memory constraints\n\n5. **Memory Management**: Each pipeline stage and executor node allocates in isolated MemoryContext, enabling efficient cleanup on error or statement completion.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nPostgreSQL implements a **classic five-stage query execution architecture** with clear separation of concerns: syntactic parsing (gram.y + scan.l), semantic analysis (analyze.c), rule rewriting (rewriteHandler.c), cost-based optimization (planner.c + allpaths.c + createplan.c with two-phase path generation and plan creation), and **Volcano-style iterator execution** (execProcnode.c with dynamic function pointer dispatch). Data flows through immutable intermediate structures (RawStmt \u2192 Query \u2192 PlannedStmt) enabling modular testing, plugin hooks, and plan caching. The executor implements pull-based pipelined execution with recursive node dispatch, where each PlanState node contains a function pointer dynamically set to its node-specific executor (ExecSeqScan, ExecNestLoop, etc.), enabling transparent wrapper instrumentation and future JIT optimization.\n\n---\n\n## Detailed References\n\n### Key Function Call Paths\n\n**Simple Query Execution**:\n```\nexec_simple_query()\n  \u2192 pg_parse_query()\n    \u2192 raw_parser() [gram.y, scan.l]\n    \u2190 RawStmt list\n  \u2192 pg_analyze_and_rewrite_fixedparams()\n    \u2192 parse_analyze_fixedparams() [analyze.c:105]\n      \u2192 transformTopLevelStmt() [analyze.c:249]\n      \u2190 Query\n    \u2192 pg_rewrite_query()\n      \u2192 QueryRewrite() [rewriteHandler.c:4566]\n      \u2190 Query list\n  \u2192 pg_plan_queries()\n    \u2192 pg_plan_query() for each query\n      \u2192 planner() [planner.c:287]\n        \u2192 standard_planner() [planner.c:303]\n          \u2192 planner_recurse_rel() [allpaths.c] \u2014 Path generation Phase 1\n          \u2192 create_plan() [createplan.c:337] \u2014 Plan creation Phase 2\n        \u2190 PlannedStmt\n  \u2192 PortalRun()\n    \u2192 ExecutorStart()\n      \u2192 ExecInitNode() [execProcnode.c:142] \u2014 Switch dispatch initialization\n    \u2192 ExecutorRun()\n      \u2192 ExecutePlan() [execMain.c:1660] \u2014 Execution loop\n        \u2192 ExecProcNode() [dynamic dispatch via function pointer]\n    \u2192 ExecutorFinish()\n    \u2192 ExecutorEnd()\n      \u2192 ExecEndNode() [execProcnode.c:562] \u2014 Switch dispatch cleanup\n```\n\n### Node Type Categories in Executor\n\n**Scan Nodes** (access tables/indexes):\n- SeqScan, IndexScan, IndexOnlyScan, BitmapHeapScan, TidScan, FunctionScan, SubqueryScan, CteScan\n\n**Join Nodes** (combine relation inputs):\n- NestLoop, MergeJoin, HashJoin\n\n**Aggregate Nodes** (reduce rows):\n- Agg, Group, WindowAgg\n\n**Materialization Nodes** (reorder or buffer):\n- Sort, Material, Memoize\n\n**Modification Nodes** (INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE):\n- ModifyTable, LockRows\n\n**Control Nodes** (control flow):\n- Result, ProjectSet, Append, MergeAppend, RecursiveUnion\n\n**Special Nodes** (optimization):\n- Gather, GatherMerge, Hash, SetOp, Limit\n\n### Optimizer Path Types\n\n```\nRelOptInfo.pathlist contains:\n  - SeqScanPath \u2014 Sequential scan of all rows\n  - IndexPath \u2014 Single index scan\n  - BitmapHeapPath \u2014 Multiple indexes combined with bitmaps\n  - NestPath \u2014 Nested loop join\n  - MergePath \u2014 Merge join\n  - HashPath \u2014 Hash join\n  - AppendPath \u2014 UNION\n  - MaterializePath \u2014 Force materialization\n  - UniquePath \u2014 Remove duplicates\n  - GroupPath \u2014 GROUP BY without aggregation\n  - UpperUniquePath, GroupUpperPath, AggPath, WindowAggPath \u2014 Upper relations\n```\n\nEach path contains cost estimates and can be converted to corresponding Plan node.\n",

# PostgreSQL Architecture - Key Insights

## Query Execution Pipeline

PostgreSQL implements a **5-stage pipeline** with clear separation of concerns:

1. **Parser** (gram.y + scan.l): Syntactic analysis → RawStmt (no DB access)
2. **Analyzer** (analyze.c): Name/type resolution → Query
3. **Rewriter** (rewriteHandler.c): Rule expansion, RLS → Query list
4. **Optimizer** (planner.c): Two-phase cost-based optimization → PlannedStmt
5. **Executor** (execProcnode.c): Volcano-style iterators → tuples

## Key Architecture Decisions

### Two-Phase Optimization
- **Phase 1** (allpaths.c): Generate all feasible paths with cost estimates
- **Phase 2** (createplan.c): Convert cheapest path → executable Plan tree
- Separation allows cheap path exploration without plan generation overhead

### Volcano-Style Execution
- Each executor node implements pull-based `ExecProcNode()` interface
- Function pointer dispatch in PlanState enables:
  - Transparent instrumentation wrapping
  - Lazy stack depth checking
  - Future JIT optimization
- Switch dispatch in ExecInitNode() creates PlanState tree mirroring Plan tree

### Expression Evaluation
- Compiled to ExprState during node initialization
- Rapid interpretation at execution time
- Can be replaced with JIT code

## Critical Files by Role

| Role | Key Files |
|------|-----------|
| Traffic Cop | `src/backend/tcop/postgres.c` |
| Parser | `src/backend/parser/{gram.y, scan.l, parser.c}` |
| Analyzer | `src/backend/parser/analyze.c` |
| Rewriter | `src/backend/rewrite/rewriteHandler.c` |
| Optimizer | `src/backend/optimizer/plan/{planner.c, allpaths.c, createplan.c}` |
| Executor | `src/backend/executor/{execMain.c, execProcnode.c, node*.c}` |
| Node Defs | `src/include/nodes/{parsenodes.h, plannodes.h, execnodes.h, pathnodes.h}` |

## Dat
